Tanzania">Population</a></th></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;2016 estimate</div></th><td>55,572,201<sup title="List of countries by Human Development Index">154th</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Currency</th><td><a href="/wiki/Tanzanian_shilling" title="Tanzanian shilling">Tanzanian shilling</a> (<a Time">UTC</a>+3</span> (<a href="/wiki/East_Africa_Time" title="East Africa Time">EAT</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand id="cite_ref-c_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-c-12">[note 1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:TZ" title=".tz">.tz</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">Revised to $41.33 billion<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup></li><li value="2">Swahili and English are <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> official languages</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Tanzania</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#716;/: secondary stress follows">&#716;</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="\'z\' in \'zoom\'">z</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/i&#720;/: \'ee\' in \'fleece\'">i&#720;</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[note 2]</a></sup> officially the <b>United Republic of Tanzania</b> (<a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>: <i lang="sw">Jamhuri ya Muungano wa Tanzania</i>), is a country in eastern Africa within the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region. It borders <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> to the north; <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> to the northeast; Comoro Islands at the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> to the east; <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a> to the south; <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the southwest; and <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the west. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a>, Africa\'s highest mountain, is in north-eastern Tanzania.\n</p><p>Some prehistoric population migrations into Tanzania include <a href="/wiki/South_Cushitic_languages" title="South Cushitic languages">Southern Cushitic</a> speakers who moved south from <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup> Eastern Cushitic people who moved into Tanzania from north of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Turkana" title="Lake Turkana">Lake Turkana</a> about 2,000 and 4,000 years ago;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Nilotic_languages" title="Southern Nilotic languages">Southern Nilotes</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Datooga_people" title="Datooga people">Datoog</a>, who originated from the present-day <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>&#8211;Ethiopia border region between 2,900 and 2,400 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 18</span></sup> These movements took place at about the same time as the settlement of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Mashariki Bantu</a> from <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> areas. They subsequently migrated across the rest of Tanzania between 2,300 and 1,700 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-18">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/European_colonialism" title="European colonialism">European colonialism</a> began in mainland Tanzania during the late 19th century when Germany formed <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a>, which gave way to British rule following <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. The mainland was governed as <a href="/wiki/Tanganyika" title="Tanganyika">Tanganyika</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Archipelago" title="Zanzibar Archipelago">Zanzibar Archipelago</a> remaining a separate colonial jurisdiction. Following their respective independence in 1961 and 1963, the two entities merged in April 1964 to form the United Republic of Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-19">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimated Tanzania\'s 2016 population at 55.57 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-7">[7]</a></sup> The population is composed of several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups" title="Ethnic groups">ethnic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Linguistic_groups" title="Linguistic groups">linguistic</a>, and religious groups. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> of Tanzania is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential" title="Presidential">presidential</a> constitutional <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> and since 1996 its official capital city has been <a href="/wiki/Dodoma" title="Dodoma">Dodoma</a> where the president\'s office, the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>, and some government ministries are located.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>, the former capital, retains most government offices and is the country\'s largest city, principal port, and leading commercial centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-19">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official_website_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-official_website-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> Tanzania is a <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system"><i>de facto</i> one-party state</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_socialism" title="Democratic socialism">democratic socialist</a> <a href="/wiki/Chama_Cha_Mapinduzi" title="Chama Cha Mapinduzi">Chama Cha Mapinduzi</a> party in power.\n</p><p>Tanzania is mountainous and densely forested in the north-east, where Mount Kilimanjaro is located. Three of <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">Africa\'s Great Lakes</a> are partly within Tanzania. To the north and west lie <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>, Africa\'s largest lake, and Lake <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Tanganyika</a>, the continent\'s deepest lake, known for its unique species of fish. The eastern shore is hot and humid, with the <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Archipelago" title="Zanzibar Archipelago">Zanzibar Archipelago</a> just offshore. The <a href="/wiki/Kalambo_Falls" title="Kalambo Falls">Kalambo Falls</a>, located on the <a href="/wiki/Kalambo_River" title="Kalambo River">Kalambo River</a> at the Zambian border, is the second highest uninterrupted <a href="/wiki/Waterfall" title="Waterfall">waterfall</a> in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalambo_Falls_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kalambo_Falls-23">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Menai_Bay_Conservation_Area" title="Menai Bay Conservation Area">Menai Bay Conservation Area</a> is Zanzibar\'s largest marine protected area.\n</p><p>Over 100 different <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Tanzania" title="Languages of Tanzania">languages are spoken in Tanzania</a>, making it the most linguistically diverse country in East Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup> The country does not have a <i>de jure</i> official language,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> although the national language is <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tzgov_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-tzgov-25">[23]</a></sup> Swahili is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary" title="Parliamentary">parliamentary</a> debate, in the lower courts, and as a medium of instruction in <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary school</a>. English is used in foreign trade, in <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a>, in higher courts, and as a medium of instruction in <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary</a> and higher education,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup> although the Tanzanian government is planning to discontinue English as a language of instruction altogether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afkinsider.com_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-afkinsider.com-26">[24]</a></sup> Approximately 10 percent of Tanzanians speak Swahili as a first language, and up to 90 percent speak it as a <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">second language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The name "Tanzania" was created as a <a href="/wiki/Clipped_compound" title="Clipped compound">clipped compound</a> of the names of the two states that unified to create the country: <a href="/wiki/Tanganyika" title="Tanganyika">Tanganyika</a> and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Zanzibar" title="People\'s Republic of Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name "Tanganyika" is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> words <i>tanga</i> ("sail") and <i>nyika</i> ("uninhabited plain", "wilderness"), creating the phrase "sail in the wilderness". It is sometimes understood as a reference to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name of Zanzibar comes from "zenji", the name for a local people (said to mean "black"), and the Arabic word "barr", which means coast or shore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tanzania" title="History of Tanzania">History of Tanzania</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Zanzibar" title="History of Zanzibar">History of Zanzibar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2625" data-file-width="2780" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_%28cropped%29.jpg/240px-Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_%28cropped%29.jpg/360px-Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_%28cropped%29.jpg/480px-Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Olduvai_stone_chopping_tool_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1.8-million-year-old stone chopping tool discovered at <a href="/wiki/Olduvai_Gorge" title="Olduvai Gorge">Olduvai Gorge</a> and currently on display at the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial">Pre-colonial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The indigenous populations of eastern Africa are thought to be the <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">linguistically isolated</a> <a href="/wiki/Hadza_people" title="Hadza people">Hadza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandawe_people" title="Sandawe people">Sandawe</a> hunter-gatherers of Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 17</span></sup>\n</p><p>The first wave of migration was by <a href="/wiki/South_Cushitic_languages" title="South Cushitic languages">Southern Cushitic</a> speakers who moved south from <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a> into Tanzania. They are ancestral to the <a href="/wiki/Iraqw_language" title="Iraqw language">Iraqw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gorowa_language" title="Gorowa language">Gorowa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Burunge_language" title="Burunge language">Burunge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 17</span></sup> Based on linguistic evidence, there may also have been two movements into Tanzania of Eastern Cushitic people at about 4,000 and 2,000 years ago, originating from north of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Turkana" title="Lake Turkana">Lake Turkana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-6"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>pages 17&#8211;18</span></sup>\n</p><p>Archaeological evidence supports the conclusion that <a href="/wiki/Southern_Nilotic_languages" title="Southern Nilotic languages">Southern Nilotes</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Datooga_people" title="Datooga people">Datoog</a>, moved south from the present-day <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> / Ethiopia border region into central northern Tanzania between 2,900 and 2,400 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-7"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 18</span></sup>\n</p><p>These movements took place at approximately the same time as the settlement of the iron-making <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Mashariki Bantu</a> from West Africa in the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a> areas. They brought with them the west African planting tradition and the primary staple of <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>. They subsequently migrated out of these regions across the rest of Tanzania between 2,300 and 1,700 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-8"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-18">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Nilotic_languages" title="Eastern Nilotic languages">Eastern Nilotic</a> peoples, including the <a href="/wiki/Maasai_people" title="Maasai people">Maasai</a>, represent a more recent migration from present-day South Sudan within the past 500 to 1,500 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Genetics_17-9"><a href="#cite_note-Genetics-17">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The people of Tanzania have been associated with the production of iron and steel. The <a href="/wiki/Pare_people" title="Pare people">Pare people</a> were the main producers of highly demanded iron for peoples who occupied the mountain regions of north-eastern Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Haya_people" title="Haya people">Haya people</a> on the western shores of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> invented a type of high-heat <a href="/wiki/Blast_furnace" title="Blast furnace">blast furnace</a>, which allowed them to forge <a href="/wiki/Carbon_steel" title="Carbon steel">carbon steel</a> at temperatures exceeding 1,820&#160;&#176;C (3,310&#160;&#176;F) more than 1,500 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Travelers and merchants from the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a> and India have visited the east African coast since early in the first millennium AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> was practiced by some on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swahili_Coast" title="Swahili Coast">Swahili Coast</a> as early as the eighth or ninth century A.D.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial">Colonial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanganyika_(territory)" title="Tanganyika (territory)">Tanganyika (territory)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:City_of_Kilwa,_1572.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1443" data-file-width="1782" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/City_of_Kilwa%2C_1572.jpg/220px-City_of_Kilwa%2C_1572.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/City_of_Kilwa%2C_1572.jpg/330px-City_of_Kilwa%2C_1572.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/City_of_Kilwa%2C_1572.jpg/440px-City_of_Kilwa%2C_1572.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:City_of_Kilwa,_1572.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1572 depiction of the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilwa" title="Kilwa">Kilwa</a>, a UNESCO World Heritage Site</div></div></div>\n<p>Claiming the coastal strip, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Omani" title="Omani">Omani</a> Sultan <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Said_bin_Sultan" title="Said bin Sultan">Said bin Sultan</a> moved his capital to <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_City" title="Zanzibar City">Zanzibar City</a> in 1840. During this time, Zanzibar became the centre for the <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Arab slave trade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> Between 65 and 90 percent of the Arab-<a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili</a> population of <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> was enslaved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> One of the most infamous slave traders on the East African coast was <a href="/wiki/Tippu_Tip" title="Tippu Tip">Tippu Tip</a>, who was the grandson of an enslaved African. The <a href="/wiki/Nyamwezi_people" title="Nyamwezi people">Nyamwezi</a> slave traders operated under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Msiri" title="Msiri">Msiri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirambo" title="Mirambo">Mirambo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Insoll" title="Timothy Insoll">Timothy Insoll</a>, "Figures record the exporting of 718,000 slaves from the Swahili coast during the 19th century, and the retention of 769,000 on the coast."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> In the 1890s, slavery was abolished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="312" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg/220px-Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg/330px-Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg/440px-Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wilhelm_Kuhnert_Schlacht_bei_Mahenge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Maji_Maji_Rebellion" title="Maji Maji Rebellion">Maji Maji Rebellion</a> against <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German</a> colonial rule in 1905</div></div></div>\n<p>In the late 19th century, Germany conquered the regions that are now Tanzania (minus Zanzibar) and incorporated them into <a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a> (GEA).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Supreme Council of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">1919 Paris Peace Conference</a> awarded all of GEA to Britain on 7 May 1919, over the strenuous objections of Belgium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ends_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ends-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>240</span></sup> The British <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Colonies" title="Secretary of State for the Colonies">colonial secretary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Milner,_1st_Viscount_Milner" title="Alfred Milner, 1st Viscount Milner">Alfred Milner</a>, and Belgium\'s minister <a href="/wiki/Plenipotentiary" title="Plenipotentiary">plenipotentiary</a> to the conference, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierre_Orts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierre Orts (page does not exist)">Pierre Orts</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pierre_Orts" title="fr:Pierre Orts">fr</a>]</span>, then negotiated the Anglo-Belgian agreement of 30 May 1919<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Belgium_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Belgium-41">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>618&#8211;9</span></sup> where Britain ceded the north-western GEA provinces of <a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda and Urundi</a> to Belgium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ends_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ends-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>246</span></sup> The conference\'s Commission on Mandates ratified this agreement on 16 July 1919.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ends_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ends-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>246&#8211;7</span></sup> The Supreme Council accepted the agreement on 7 August 1919.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Belgium_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Belgium-41">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>612&#8211;3</span></sup> On 12 July 1919, the Commission on Mandates agreed that the small <a href="/wiki/Kionga_Triangle" title="Kionga Triangle">Kionga Triangle</a> south of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rovuma_River" title="Rovuma River">Rovuma River</a> would be given to <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mozambique" title="Portuguese Mozambique">Portuguese Mozambique</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ends_40-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ends-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>243</span></sup> with it eventually becoming part of independent <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>. The commission reasoned that Germany had virtually forced Portugal to cede the triangle in 1894.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ends_40-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ends-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>243</span></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> was signed on 28 July 1919, although the treaty did not take effect until 10 January 1920. On that date, the GEA was transferred officially to Britain, Belgium, and Portugal. Also on that date, "Tanganyika" became the name of the British territory.\n</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, about 100,000 people from Tanganyika joined the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied forces</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heale_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heale-42">[40]</a></sup> and were among the 375,000 Africans who fought with those forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGT_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-MGT-43">[41]</a></sup> Tanganyikans fought in units of the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_African_Rifles" title="King\'s African Rifles">King\'s African Rifles</a> during the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="East African Campaign (World War II)">East African Campaign</a> in <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Abyssinia</a> against the Italians, in <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vichy_French" title="Vichy French">Vichy French</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madagascar" title="Battle of Madagascar">Madagascar Campaign</a>, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burma" title="Burma">Burma</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japanese</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Burma_Campaign_1944%E2%80%9345" title="Burma Campaign 1944&#8211;45">Burma Campaign</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MGT_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-MGT-43">[41]</a></sup> Tanganyika was an important source of food during this war, and its export income increased greatly compared to the pre-war years of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heale_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Heale-42">[40]</a></sup> Wartime demand, however, caused increased commodity prices and massive <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a> within the colony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1954, <a href="/wiki/Julius_Nyerere" title="Julius Nyerere">Julius Nyerere</a> transformed an organisation into the politically oriented <a href="/wiki/Tanganyika_African_National_Union" title="Tanganyika African National Union">Tanganyika African National Union</a> (TANU). TANU\'s main objective was to achieve national <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> for Tanganyika. A campaign to register new members was launched, and within a year, TANU had become the leading political organisation in the country. Nyerere became Minister of British-administered Tanganyika in 1960 and continued as prime minister when Tanganyika became independent in 1961.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-colonial">Post-colonial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-colonial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>British rule came to an end on 9 December 1961, but for the first year of independence, Tanganyika had a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_general" title="Governor general">governor general</a> who represented the British monarch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 6</span></sup> On 9 December 1962, Tanganyika became a democratic republic under an executive president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 6</span></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Revolution" title="Zanzibar Revolution">Zanzibar Revolution</a> overthrew the Arab dynasty in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar-46">[44]</a></sup> which had become independent in 1963, the archipelago merged with mainland Tanganyika on 26 April 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> On 29 October of the same year, the country was renamed the United Republic of Tanzania ("Tan" comes from Tanganyika and "Zan" from Zanzibar).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-19">[17]</a></sup> The union of the two hitherto separate regions was controversial among many Zanzibaris (even those sympathetic to the revolution) but was accepted by both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nyerere" title="Nyerere">Nyerere</a> government and the Revolutionary Government of Zanzibar owing to shared political values and goals.\n</p><p>Following Tanganyika\'s independence and unification with Zanzibar leading to the state of Tanzania, President Nyerere emphasized a need to construct a national identity for the citizens of the new country. To achieve this, Nyerere provided what is regarded as one of the most successful cases of ethnic repression and identity transformation in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> With over 130 languages spoken within its territory, Tanzania is one of the most ethnically diverse countries in Africa. Despite this obstacle, ethnic divisions remained rare in Tanzania when compared to the rest of the continent, notably its immediate neighbor, Kenya. Furthermore, since its independence, Tanzania has displayed more political stability than most African countries, particularly due to Nyerere\'s ethnic repression methods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg/220px-Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg/330px-Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg/440px-Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arusha_Declaration_Monument.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Declaration_Monument" title="Arusha Declaration Monument">Arusha Declaration Monument</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1967, Nyerere\'s first presidency took a turn to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_politics" title="Left politics">left</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Declaration" title="Arusha Declaration">Arusha Declaration</a>, which codified a commitment to socialism as well-as <a href="/wiki/Pan-Africanism" title="Pan-Africanism">Pan-Africanism</a>. After the declaration, banks and many large industries were nationalised.\n</p><p>Tanzania was also aligned with China, which from 1970 to 1975 financed and helped build the 1,860-kilometre-long (1,160&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/TAZARA_Railway" title="TAZARA Railway">TAZARA Railway</a> from Dar es Salaam to <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> Nonetheless, from the late 1970s, Tanzania\'s economy took a turn for the worse, in the context of an international economic crisis affecting both developed and developing economies.\n</p><p>From the mid-1980s, the regime financed itself by borrowing from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> and underwent some reforms. Since then, Tanzania\'s gross domestic product per capita has grown and poverty has been reduced, according to a report by the World Bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1992, the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Tanzania" title="Constitution of Tanzania">Constitution of Tanzania</a> was amended to allow multiple political parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> In Tanzania\'s first multi-party elections, held in 1995, the ruling <a href="/wiki/Chama_Cha_Mapinduzi" title="Chama Cha Mapinduzi">Chama Cha Mapinduzi</a> won 186 of the 232 elected seats in the National Assembly, and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Mkapa" title="Benjamin Mkapa">Benjamin Mkapa</a> was elected as president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Tanzania" title="Geography of Tanzania">Geography of Tanzania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Archipelago" title="Zanzibar Archipelago">Zanzibar Archipelago</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:348px;max-width:348px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Elephant_and_Kilimanjaro.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="851" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Elephant_and_Kilimanjaro.jpg/180px-Elephant_and_Kilimanjaro.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Elephant_and_Kilimanjaro.jpg/270px-Elephant_and_Kilimanjaro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Elephant_and_Kilimanjaro.jpg/360px-Elephant_and_Kilimanjaro.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">An elephant passing by the snow-capped <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt._Kilimanjaro" title="Mt. Kilimanjaro">Mt. Kilimanjaro</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ngorongoro_Crater.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ngorongoro_Crater.jpg/160px-Ngorongoro_Crater.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ngorongoro_Crater.jpg/240px-Ngorongoro_Crater.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Ngorongoro_Crater.jpg/320px-Ngorongoro_Crater.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ngorongoro_Crater" title="Ngorongoro Crater">Ngorongoro Crater</a>, the world\'s largest inactive and intact volcanic <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">caldera</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tanzania_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tanzania map of K&#246;ppen climate classification</div></div></div>\n<p>At 947,303 square kilometres (365,756&#160;sq&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BFF_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-BFF-6">[6]</a></sup> Tanzania is the 13th largest country in Africa and the 31st largest in the world, ranked between the larger <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and smaller <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Size_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Size-54">[52]</a></sup> It borders <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> to the north; <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> to the west; and <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> to the south. Tanzania is located on the eastern coast of Africa and has an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> coastline approximately 1,424 kilometres (885&#160;mi) long.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> It also incorporates several offshore islands, including <a href="/wiki/Unguja" title="Unguja">Unguja</a> (Zanzibar), <a href="/wiki/Pemba_Island" title="Pemba Island">Pemba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mafia_Island" title="Mafia Island">Mafia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1245</span></sup> The country is the site of Africa\'s highest and lowest points: <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a>, at 5,895 metres (19,341&#160;ft) above sea level, and the floor of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tanganyika" title="Lake Tanganyika">Lake Tanganyika</a>, at 352 metres (1,155&#160;ft) below sea level, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1245</span></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park,_Tanzania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1776" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park%2C_Tanzania.jpg/230px-Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park%2C_Tanzania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park%2C_Tanzania.jpg/345px-Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park%2C_Tanzania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park%2C_Tanzania.jpg/460px-Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park%2C_Tanzania.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wildebeest_Migration_in_Serengeti_National_Park,_Tanzania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wildebeest migration in the <a href="/wiki/Serengeti" title="Serengeti">Serengeti</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Tanzania is mountainous and densely forested in the northeast, where Mount Kilimanjaro is located. Three of <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">Africa\'s Great Lakes</a> are partly within Tanzania. To the north and west lie <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a>, Africa\'s largest lake, and Lake Tanganyika, the continent\'s deepest lake, known for its unique species of fish. To the southwest lies <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Nyasa" title="Lake Nyasa">Lake Nyasa</a>. Central Tanzania is a large plateau, with plains and arable land. The eastern shore is hot and humid, with the <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Archipelago" title="Zanzibar Archipelago">Zanzibar Archipelago</a> just offshore.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kalambo_Falls" title="Kalambo Falls">Kalambo Falls</a> in the southwestern region of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rukwa" title="Rukwa">Rukwa</a> is the second highest uninterrupted waterfall in Africa, and is located near the southeastern shore of Lake Tanganyika on the border with Zambia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kalambo_Falls_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kalambo_Falls-23">[21]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Menai_Bay_Conservation_Area" title="Menai Bay Conservation Area">Menai Bay Conservation Area</a> is Zanzibar\'s largest marine protected area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Tanzania" title="Climate of Tanzania">Climate of Tanzania</a></div>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This paragraph <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br/><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Tanzania%22" rel="nofollow">"Tanzania"</a>&#160;&#8211;&#160;<a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Tanzania%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">news</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Tanzania%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Tanzania%22+-wikipedia" rel="nofollow">books</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Tanzania%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <a class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Tanzania%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Climate varies greatly within Tanzania. In the highlands, temperatures range between 10 and 20&#160;&#176;C (50 and 68&#160;&#176;F) during cold and hot seasons respectively. The rest of the country has temperatures rarely falling lower than 20&#160;&#176;C (68&#160;&#176;F). The hottest period extends between November and February (25&#8211;31&#160;&#176;C or 77.0&#8211;87.8&#160;&#176;F) while the coldest period occurs between May and August (15&#8211;20&#160;&#176;C or 59&#8211;68&#160;&#176;F). Annual temperature is 20&#160;&#176;C (68.0&#160;&#176;F). The climate is cool in high mountainous regions.\n</p><p>Tanzania has two major rainfall regimes: one is uni-modal (October&#8211;April) and the other is bi-modal (October&#8211;December and March&#8211;May).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-rain-57">[55]</a></sup> The former is experienced in southern, central, and western parts of the country, and the latter is found in the north from <a href="/wiki/Lake_Victoria" title="Lake Victoria">Lake Victoria</a> extending east to the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-rain-57">[55]</a></sup> The bi-modal regime is caused by the seasonal migration of the <a href="/wiki/Intertropical_Convergence_Zone" title="Intertropical Convergence Zone">Intertropical Convergence Zone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-rain-57">[55]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife_and_conservation">Wildlife and conservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Wildlife and conservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Tanzania" title="Wildlife of Tanzania">Wildlife of Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1981" data-file-width="2965" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg/230px-Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg/345px-Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg/460px-Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giraffes_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tower of giraffes at <a href="/wiki/Arusha_National_Park" title="Arusha National Park">Arusha National Park</a>. The giraffe is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_animal" title="National animal">national animal</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Approximately 38 percent of Tanzania\'s land area is set aside in protected areas for conservation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> Tanzania has 16 national parks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup> plus a variety of game and forest reserves, including the <a href="/wiki/Ngorongoro_Conservation_Area" title="Ngorongoro Conservation Area">Ngorongoro Conservation Area</a>. In western Tanzania, <a href="/wiki/Gombe_Stream_National_Park" title="Gombe Stream National Park">Gombe Stream National Park</a> is the site of <a href="/wiki/Jane_Goodall" title="Jane Goodall">Jane Goodall</a>\'s ongoing study of <a href="/wiki/Common_chimpanzee" title="Common chimpanzee">chimpanzee</a> behaviour, which started in 1960.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania is highly biodiverse and contains a wide variety of animal habitats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> On Tanzania\'s <a href="/wiki/Serengeti" title="Serengeti">Serengeti</a> plain, white-bearded <a href="/wiki/Wildebeest" title="Wildebeest">wildebeest</a> (<i>Connochaetes taurinus mearnsi</i>) and other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bovid" title="Bovid">bovids</a> participate in a large-scale annual migration. Tanzania is home to about 130 amphibian and over 275 reptile species, many of them strictly endemic and included in the <a href="/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature" title="International Union for Conservation of Nature">International Union for Conservation of Nature</a>\'s Red Lists of countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Tanzania" title="Politics of Tanzania">Politics of Tanzania</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Tanzania" title="Constitution of Tanzania">Constitution of Tanzania</a></div>\n<p>Tanzania is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/One_party_dominant_state" title="One party dominant state">one party dominant state</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Chama_Cha_Mapinduzi" title="Chama Cha Mapinduzi">Chama Cha Mapinduzi</a> (CCM) party in power. From its formation until 1992, it was the only legally permitted party in the country. This changed on 1 July 1992, when the constitution was amended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 3</span></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Magufuli" title="John Magufuli">John Magufuli</a> won the October 2015 presidential election and secured a two-thirds majority in parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> The other party or main opposition party<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (December 2017)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup> in Tanzania is called <a href="/wiki/Chadema" title="Chadema">Chama cha Demokrasia na Maendeleo (Chadema)</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> for "Party for Democracy and Progress"). In Zanzibar, the <a href="/wiki/Civic_United_Front" title="Civic United Front">Civil United Front (CUF)</a> is considered a main opposition political party.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive">Executive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Executive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:225px;max-width:225px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:110px;max-width:110px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Magufuli_2015.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="282" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/John_Magufuli_2015.png/108px-John_Magufuli_2015.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/John_Magufuli_2015.png/162px-John_Magufuli_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/John_Magufuli_2015.png/216px-John_Magufuli_2015.png 2x" width="108"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/John_Magufuli" title="John Magufuli">President John Magufuli</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:111px;max-width:111px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1805" data-file-width="1333" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg/109px-Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg/164px-Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg/218px-Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg 2x" width="109"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Kassim_Majaliwa" title="Kassim Majaliwa">Prime Minister Kassim Majaliwa</a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Tanzania" title="President of Tanzania">president of Tanzania</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Tanzania_National_Assembly_members" title="List of Tanzania National Assembly members">members of the National Assembly</a> are elected concurrently by direct popular vote for five-year terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 42(2)</span></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Tanzania" title="Vice President of Tanzania">vice-president</a> is elected for a five-year term at the same time as the president and on the same ticket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167;&#167; 47(2), 50(1)</span></sup> Neither the president nor the vice-president may be a member of the National Assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 66(2)</span></sup> The president appoints a <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Tanzania" title="Prime Minister of Tanzania">prime minister</a>, subject to confirmation by the assembly, to serve as the government\'s leader in the assembly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-4"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167;&#167; 51(1)-(2), 52(2)</span></sup> The president selects his or her <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Tanzania" title="Cabinet of Tanzania">cabinet</a> from assembly members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-5"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 55</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislature">Legislature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Legislature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>All legislative power relating to mainland Tanzania and union matters is vested in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Tanzania" title="National Assembly of Tanzania">National Assembly</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-6"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 64(1)</span></sup> which is unicameral and has a maximum of 357 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edge-66">[64]</a></sup> These include members elected to represent constituencies, the attorney general, five members elected by the <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> house of representatives from among its own members, the special women\'s seats that constitute at least 30% of the seats that any party has in the assembly, the speaker of the assembly (if not otherwise a member of the assembly), and the persons (not more than ten) appointed by the president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-7"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 66(1)</span></sup> The Tanzania Electoral Commission demarcates the mainland into constituencies in the number determined by the commission with the consent of the president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-8"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 75</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Tanzania" title="Chief Justice of Tanzania">Chief Justice of Tanzania</a></div>\n<p>Tanzania\'s legal system is based on English <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania has a four-level judiciary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup> The lowest-level courts on the Tanzanian mainland are the Primary Courts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup> In Zanzibar, the lowest-level courts are the Kadhi\'s Courts for Islamic family matters and the Primary Courts for all other cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-3"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup> On the mainland, appeal is to either the District Courts or the Resident Magistrates Courts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-4"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup> In Zanzibar, appeal is to the Kadhi\'s Appeal Courts for Islamic family matters and the Magistrates Courts for all other cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-5"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup> From there, appeal is to the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Tanzania" title="High Court of Tanzania">High Court of Mainland Tanzania or Zanzibar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-6"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup> No appeal regarding Islamic family matters can be made from the High Court of Zanzibar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-7"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 99(1)</span></sup> Otherwise, the final appeal is to the Court of Appeal of Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-8"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The High Court of mainland Tanzania has three divisions &#8211; commercial, labour, and land<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_67-9"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-67">[65]</a></sup> &#8211; and 15 geographic zones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> The High Court of Zanzibar has an industrial division, which hears only labour disputes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mainland and union judges are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Tanzania" title="Chief Justice of Tanzania">Chief Justice of Tanzania</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> except for those of the Court of Appeal and the High Court, who are appointed by the president of Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-9"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span> &#167;&#167; 109(1), 118(2)&#8211;(3)</span></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania is a party to the <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Tanzania" title="Human rights in Tanzania">Human rights in Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_people_with_albinism" title="Persecution of people with albinism">Persecution of people with albinism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Tanzania" title="LGBT rights in Tanzania">LGBT rights in Tanzania</a></div>\n<p>Throughout Tanzania, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_by_country_or_territory" title="LGBT rights by country or territory">sex acts between men</a> are illegal and carry a maximum penalty of life imprisonment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> According to a 2007 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> survey, 95 percent of Tanzanians believed that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup>\n</p><p>People with <a href="/wiki/Albinism" title="Albinism">albinism</a> living in Tanzania are often attacked, killed or mutilated because of superstitions related to the black-magical practice known as <a href="/wiki/Muti" title="Muti">muti</a> that say body parts of albinos have magical properties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania has the highest occurrence of this human rights violation among 27 African countries where muti is known to be practised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Zanzibar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spice_Islands_(Zanzibar_highlighted)_sv.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="879" data-file-width="713" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg/170px-Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg/255px-Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg/340px-Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spice_Islands_(Zanzibar_highlighted)_sv.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Archipelago" title="Zanzibar Archipelago">Zanzibar Archipelago</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The legislative authority in Zanzibar over all non-union matters is vested in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Zanzibar)" title="House of Representatives (Zanzibar)">House of Representatives</a> (per the Tanzania constitution)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-10"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 106(3)</span></sup> or the Legislative Council (per the Zanzibar constitution).\n</p><p>The Legislative Council has two parts: the president of Zanzibar and the House of Representatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_64-11"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 107(1)-(2)</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 63(1)</span></sup> The president is Zanzibar\'s head of government and the chairman of the Revolutionary Council, in which the executive authority of Zanzibar is invested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167;&#167; 5A(2), 26(1)</span></sup> Zanzibar has two vice-presidents, with the first being from the main opposition party in the house.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eisa_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa-77">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Troubled_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Troubled-78">[76]</a></sup> The second is from the party in power and is the leader of government business in the House.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Troubled_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Troubled-78">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The president and the members of the House of Representatives have five-year terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 28(2)</span></sup>\n</p><p>The president selects ministers from members of the House of Representatives,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-4"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 42(2)</span></sup> with the ministers allocated according to the number of House seats won by political parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eisa_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa-77">[75]</a></sup> The Revolutionary Council consists of the president, both vice-presidents, all ministers, the attorney general of Zanzibar, and other house members deemed fit by the president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eisa_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa-77">[75]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The House of Representatives is composed of elected members, ten members appointed by the president, all the regional commissioners of Zanzibar, the attorney general, and appointed female members whose number must be equal to 30 percent of the elected members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-5"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167;&#167; 55(3), 64, 67(1)</span></sup> The House determines the number of its elected members<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-6"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 120(2)</span></sup> with the Zanzibar Electoral Commission determining the boundaries of each election constituency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_68-7"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>&#167; 120(1)</span></sup> In 2013, the House had 81 members: fifty elected members, five regional commissioners, the attorney general, ten members appointed by the president, and fifteen appointed female members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edge_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Edge-66">[64]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_subdivisions">Administrative subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Tanzania" title="Regions of Tanzania">Regions of Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Tanzania" title="Districts of Tanzania">Districts of Tanzania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Tanzania" title="Subdivisions of Tanzania">Subdivisions of Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tanzania,_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_(%2Bdetails).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2947" data-file-width="3096" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg/220px-Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg/330px-Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg/440px-Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tanzania,_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_(%2Bdetails).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regions of Tanzania</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1972, local government on the mainland was abolished and replaced with direct rule from the central government. Local government, however, was reintroduced in the beginning of the 1980s, when the rural councils and rural authorities were re-established. Local government elections took place in 1983, and functioning councils started in 1984. In 1999, a Local Government Reform Programme was enacted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>, setting "a comprehensive and ambitious agenda ... [covering] four areas: political decentralization, financial decentralization, administrative decentralization and changed central-local relations, with the mainland government having over-riding powers within the framework of the Constitution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunnat_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kunnat-79">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2016, Tanzania is divided into thirty-one regions. <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Tanzania" title="Regions of Tanzania">regions</a> (<i>mkoa</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> twenty-six on the mainland and five in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> (three on <a href="/wiki/Unguja" title="Unguja">Unguja</a>, two on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pemba,_Tanzania" title="Pemba, Tanzania">Pemba</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> In 2012, the thirty former regions were divided into 169 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Tanzania" title="Districts of Tanzania">districts</a> (wilaya), also known as local government authorities. Of those districts, 34 were urban units, which were further classified as three city councils (<a href="/wiki/Arusha" title="Arusha">Arusha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbeya" title="Mbeya">Mbeya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mwanza" title="Mwanza">Mwanza</a>), nineteen municipal councils, and twelve town councils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012_census_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-2012_census-8">[8]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The urban units have an autonomous city, municipal, or town council and are subdivided into wards and <i>mtaa</i>. The non-urban units have an autonomous district council but are subdivided into village councils or township authorities (first level) and then into <i>vitongoji</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunnat_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kunnat-79">[77]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city of Dar es Salaam is unique because it has a city council whose areal jurisdiction overlaps three municipal councils. The mayor of the city council is elected by that council. The twenty-member city council is composed of eleven persons elected by the municipal councils, seven members of the National Assembly, and "Nominated members of parliament under \'Special Seats\' for women". Each municipal council also has a mayor. "The City Council performs a coordinating role and attends to issues cutting across the three municipalities", including security and emergency services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> The city of Mwanza has a city council whose areal jurisdiction overlaps two municipal councils.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Tanzania" title="Foreign relations of Tanzania">Foreign relations of Tanzania</a></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bilateral_relations">Bilateral relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Bilateral relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="2388"
