decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG/170px-Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG/255px-Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG/340px-Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Tanzania,_Washington,_D.C." title="Embassy of Tanzania, Washington, D.C.">Tanzanian Embassy</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_End,_Washington,_D.C." title="West End, Washington, D.C.">West End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, USA</div></div></div>\n<p>Apart from its border dispute with Malawi, Tanzania had cordial relations with its neighbours in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-year_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-year-85">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Malawi%E2%80%93Tanzania_relations" title="Malawi&#8211;Tanzania relations">Relations between Tanzania and Malawi</a> have been tense because of a <a href="/wiki/Lake_Malawi#Tanzania&#8211;Malawi_dispute" title="Lake Malawi">dispute</a> over the countries\' <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lake_Nyasa" title="Lake Nyasa">Lake Nyasa</a> (Lake Malawi) border. An unsuccessful mediation regarding this issue took place in March 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-year_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-year-85">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllAfrica.com_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-AllAfrica.com-86">[84]</a></sup> The two countries agreed in 2013 to ask the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> (ICJ) to resolve the dispute should mediation be unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tvcnews.tv_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-tvcnews.tv-87">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, but not Tanzania, has accepted the compulsory jurisdiction of the ICJ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icj-cij.org_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-icj-cij.org-88">[86]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rwanda%E2%80%93Tanzania_relations" title="Rwanda&#8211;Tanzania relations">Relations between Tanzania and Rwanda</a> deteriorated in 2013 when Tanzanian President <a href="/wiki/Jakaya_Kikwete" title="Jakaya Kikwete">Jakaya Kikwete</a> said that if the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (DRC) could negotiate with some of its enemies, Rwanda should be able to do the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> Rwandan President <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kagame" title="Paul Kagame">Paul Kagame</a> then expressed "contempt" for Kikwete\'s statement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> The tension was renewed in May 2014 when, in a speech to the Tanzanian <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>, Foreign Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Membe" title="Bernard Membe">Bernard Membe</a> renewed his claim that Rwandans were causing instability in the DRC. Rwandan Foreign Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/Louise_Mushikiwabo" title="Louise Mushikiwabo">Louise Mushikiwabo</a> responded, "As for Tanzania\'s foreign minister whose anti-Rwanda rant in parliament I heard, he would benefit from a lesson in the history of the region."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tanzania%E2%80%93China_relations" title="Tanzania&#8211;China relations">Tanzania&#8211;China relations</a> have strengthened in recent years as trade between the two countries and Chinese investment in Tanzanian infrastructure have increased rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-3"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tanzania%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Tanzania&#8211;United States relations">Relations with the United States</a> are warm, with President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_presidential_trips_made_by_Barack_Obama" title="List of presidential trips made by Barack Obama">visiting Tanzania</a> in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-94">[92]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania\'s relations with other donor countries, including <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> and members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, are generally good, though donors are concerned about Tanzania\'s commitment to reducing government corruption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-4"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-year_85-2"><a href="#cite_note-year-85">[83]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Multilateral_relations">Multilateral relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Multilateral relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Tanzania is a member of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC), along with Uganda, Kenya, Rwanda, and Burundi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> According to the East African Common Market Protocol of 2010, the free trade and free movement of people is guaranteed, including the right to reside in another member country for purposes of employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-5"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>1250</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup> This protocol, however, has not been implemented because of work permit and other bureaucratic, legal, and financial obstacles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> The EAC, the SADC, and the <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa</a> agreed in June 2011 to negotiate the creation of a Tripartite Free Trade Area spanning 26 African countries, with a goal to complete the first phase of negotiations within 36 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 31 October 2014, Tanzania was contributing 2,253 soldiers and other personnel to various <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> peacekeeping operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_People%27s_Defence_Force" title="Tanzania People\'s Defence Force">Tanzanian military</a> is participating along with South African and Malawian militaries in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">United Nations Force Intervention Brigade</a> (MONUSCO) in the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> (DRC). The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> authorised the force on 28 March 2013 to conduct targeted offensive operations to neutralise groups that threaten peace in the DRC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> Tanzania was also participating in peacekeeping missions in the <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur Region</a> of Sudan (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNAMID" title="UNAMID">UNAMID</a>); <a href="/wiki/Abyei" title="Abyei">Abyei</a>, control of which is contested between South Sudan and Sudan (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNISFA" title="UNISFA">UNISFA</a>); the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> (MINUSCA); <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNIFIL" title="UNIFIL">UNIFIL</a>); and South Sudan (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNMISS" title="UNMISS">UNMISS</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FIB-training-22_(9311333487).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="834" data-file-width="1250" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg/220px-FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg/330px-FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg/440px-FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FIB-training-22_(9311333487).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tanzanian special forces during a training exercise</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_People%27s_Defence_Force" title="Tanzania People\'s Defence Force">Tanzania People\'s Defence Force</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Tanzania" title="Economy of Tanzania">Economy of Tanzania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Tanzania" title="Poverty in Tanzania">Poverty in Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg/220px-Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg/330px-Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg/440px-Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_Tanzania_golden_hour.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Tanzania" title="Bank of Tanzania">Bank of Tanzania Twin Towers</a></div></div></div>\n<p>As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, according to the IMF, Tanzania\'s <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) was an estimated $56.7 billion (nominal), or $176.5 billion on a <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) basis. GDP per capita (PPP) was $3,457.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2009 through 2013, Tanzania\'s per capita GDP (based on constant local currency) grew an average of 3.5% per year, higher than any other member of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC) and exceeded by only nine countries in Sub-Saharan Africa: the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania\'s largest trading partners in 2012 for its US$5.5 billion in exports were <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UND_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-UND-106">[104]</a></sup> Its imports totalled US$11.7 billion, with Switzerland, China, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> being the biggest partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UND_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-UND-106">[104]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG/220px-The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG/330px-The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG/440px-The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kariakoo" title="Kariakoo">Kariakoo</a> market in Dar es Salaam</div></div></div>\n<p>Tanzania weathered the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>, which began in late 2008 or early 2009, relatively well. Strong gold prices, bolstering the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Tanzania" title="Mining industry of Tanzania">mining industry</a>, and Tanzania\'s poor integration into global markets helped to insulate the country from the downturn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-6"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup> Since the recession ended, the Tanzanian economy has expanded rapidly thanks to strong tourism, telecommunications, and banking sectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-7"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup>\n</p><p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" title="United Nations Development Program">United Nations Development Program</a>, however, recent growth in the national economy has benefited only the "very few", leaving out the majority of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> Tanzania\'s 2013 <a href="/wiki/Global_Hunger_Index" title="Global Hunger Index">Global Hunger Index</a> was worse than any other country in the EAC except <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHI_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-GHI-108">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 15</span></sup> The proportion of persons who were undernourished in 2010&#8211;12 was also worse than any other EAC country except Burundi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHI_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-GHI-108">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 51</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="More_about_Tanzania">More about Tanzania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: More about Tanzania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_UNDP_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania_UNDP-109">[107]</a></sup> Tanzania has made little progress towards reducing extreme hunger and malnutrition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_UNDP_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania_UNDP-109">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-110">[108]</a></sup> The 2010 Global Hunger Index ranks the situation as &#8220;alarming&#8221;.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_UNDP_109-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania_UNDP-109">[107]</a></sup> Children in rural areas suffer substantially higher rates of malnutrition and chronic hunger, although urban-rural disparities have narrowed as regards both stunting and underweight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_UNDP_109-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania_UNDP-109">[107]</a></sup> Low rural sector productivity arises mainly from inadequate infrastructure investment; limited access to farm inputs, extension services and credit; limited technology as well as trade and marketing support; and heavy dependence on rain-fed agriculture and natural resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_UNDP_109-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania_UNDP-109">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Approximately 68 percent of Tanzania\'s 44.9 million citizens live below the poverty line of $1.25 a day and 16 percent of children under 5 are malnourished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-110">[108]</a></sup> The most prominent challenges Tanzania faces in poverty reduction are unsustainable harvesting of its natural resources, unchecked cultivation, climate change and water- source encroachment, according to the United Nations Development Programme (UNDP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-110">[108]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are very few resources for Tanzanians in terms of credit services, infrastructure or availability to improved agricultural technologies, which further exacerbates hunger and poverty in the country according to the UNDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_110-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-110">[108]</a></sup> Tanzania ranks 159 out of 187 countries in poverty according to the United Nation\'s Human Development Index (2014).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tanzania_110-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-110">[108]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Tanzania" title="Agriculture in Tanzania">Agriculture in Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tea_fields,_Tukuyu,_Tanzania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg/220px-Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg/330px-Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg/440px-Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tea_fields,_Tukuyu,_Tanzania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tea fields in Tukuyu</div></div></div>\n<p>The Tanzanian economy is heavily based on agriculture, which in 2013 accounted for 24.5 percent of gross domestic product,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-2"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 37</span></sup> provides 85% of exports,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-19">[17]</a></sup> and accounted for half of the employed workforce;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-3"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 56</span></sup> The agricultural sector grew 4.3 percent in 2012, less than half of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goal" title="Millennium Development Goal">Millennium Development Goal</a> target of 10.8%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> 16.4 percent of the land is <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> with 2.4 percent of the land planted with <a href="/wiki/Permanent_crop" title="Permanent crop">permanent crops</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> Tanzania\'s economy relies on farming, but climate change has impacted their farming.\n</p><p>Maize was the largest food crop on the Tanzania mainland in 2013 (5.17 million tonnes), followed by cassava (1.94 million tonnes), sweet potatoes (1.88 million tonnes), beans (1.64 million tonnes), bananas (1.31 million tonnes), rice (1.31 million tonnes), and millet (1.04 million tonnes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-4"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 58</span></sup> Sugar was the largest <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crop</a> on the mainland in 2013 (296,679 tonnes), followed by cotton (241,198 tonnes), cashew nuts (126,000 tonnes), tobacco (86,877 tonnes), coffee (48,000 tonnes), sisal (37,368 tonnes), and tea (32,422 tonnes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-5"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 58</span></sup> Beef was the largest meat product on the mainland in 2013 (299,581 tonnes), followed by lamb/mutton (115,652 tonnes), chicken (87,408 tonnes), and pork (50,814 tonnes).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-6"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 60</span></sup>\n</p><p>According to the 2002 National Irrigation Master Plan, 29.4 million hectares in Tanzania are suitable for irrigation farming; however, only 310,745 hectares were actually being irrigated in June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Industry.2C_energy_and_construction"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry,_energy_and_construction">Industry, energy and construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Industry, energy and construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Tanzania" title="Energy in Tanzania">Energy in Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Tanzania" title="Water supply and sanitation in Tanzania">Water supply and sanitation in Tanzania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource_and_waste_management_in_Tanzania" title="Natural resource and waste management in Tanzania">Natural resource and waste management in Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Tanzania" title="List of companies of Tanzania">List of companies of Tanzania</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Williamson_Diamond_Mine,_Mwazui,_Tanzania.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Williamson_Diamond_Mine%2C_Mwazui%2C_Tanzania.JPG/200px-Williamson_Diamond_Mine%2C_Mwazui%2C_Tanzania.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Williamson_Diamond_Mine%2C_Mwazui%2C_Tanzania.JPG/300px-Williamson_Diamond_Mine%2C_Mwazui%2C_Tanzania.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Williamson_Diamond_Mine%2C_Mwazui%2C_Tanzania.JPG/400px-Williamson_Diamond_Mine%2C_Mwazui%2C_Tanzania.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Williamson_diamond_mine" title="Williamson diamond mine">Williamson diamond mine</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Songo_Songo_Gas_Plant.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Songo_Songo_Gas_Plant.jpg/200px-Songo_Songo_Gas_Plant.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Songo_Songo_Gas_Plant.jpg/300px-Songo_Songo_Gas_Plant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Songo_Songo_Gas_Plant.jpg/400px-Songo_Songo_Gas_Plant.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Songo_Songo_Island" title="Songo Songo Island">Songo Songo</a> Gas Plant</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Industry and construction is a major and growing component of the Tanzanian economy, contributing 22.2 percent of GDP in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-7"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 37</span></sup> This component includes mining and quarrying, manufacturing, electricity and natural gas, water supply, and construction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-8"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 37</span></sup> Mining contributed 3.3 percent of GDP in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-9"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 33</span></sup> The vast majority of the country\'s mineral export revenue comes from gold, accounting for 89 percent of the value of those exports in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-10"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 71</span></sup> It also exports sizeable quantities of gemstones, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diamonds" title="Diamonds">diamonds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanzanite" title="Tanzanite">tanzanite</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-8"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1251</span></sup> All of Tanzania\'s <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> production, which totalled 106,000 short tons in 2012, is used domestically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIA_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-115">[113]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Only 15 percent of Tanzanians had access to electric power in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-data.worldbank.org_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-data.worldbank.org-116">[114]</a></sup> The government-owned <a href="/wiki/TANESCO" title="TANESCO">Tanzania Electric Supply Company Limited</a> (TANESCO) dominates the electric supply industry in Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWURA-El_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-EWURA-El-117">[115]</a></sup> The country generated 6.013 billion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt_hours" title="Kilowatt hours">kilowatt hours</a> (kWh) of electricity in 2013, a 4.2 percent increase over the 5.771 billion kWh generated in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BudEx_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-BudEx-118">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 4</span></sup> Generation increased by 63 percent between 2005 and 2012;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012Elec_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-2012Elec-119">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> Almost 18 percent of the electricity generated in 2012 was lost because of theft and transmission and distribution problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012Elec_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-2012Elec-119">[117]</a></sup> The electrical supply varies, particularly when droughts disrupt hydropower electric generation; rolling blackouts are implemented as necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-9"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1251</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWURA-El_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-EWURA-El-117">[115]</a></sup> The unreliability of the electrical supply has hindered the development of Tanzanian industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-10"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1251</span></sup> In 2013, 49.7 percent of Tanzania\'s electricity generation came from natural gas, 28.9 percent from hydroelectric sources, 20.4 percent from thermal sources, and 1.0 percent from outside the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BudEx_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-BudEx-118">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 5</span></sup> The government has built a 532 kilometres (331&#160;mi) gas pipeline from <a href="/wiki/Mnazi_Bay-Ruvuma_Estuary_Marine_Park" title="Mnazi Bay-Ruvuma Estuary Marine Park">Mnazi Bay</a> to Dar es Salaam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> This pipeline was expected to allow the country to double its electricity generation capacity to 3,000 megawatts by 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> The government\'s goal is to increase capacity to at least 10,000 megawatts by 2025.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg/220px-Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg/330px-Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg/440px-Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nyerere_Bridge_-_Kigamboni_.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nyerere Bridge in Kigamboni, Dar es Salaam, is Tanzania\'s (and East Africa\'s) only suspension bridge.</div></div></div>\n<p>According to <a href="/wiki/PFC_Energy" title="PFC Energy">PFC Energy</a>, 25 to 30 trillion cubic feet of recoverable natural gas resources have been discovered in Tanzania since 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EIA_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-115">[113]</a></sup> bringing the total reserves to over 43 trillion cubic feet by the end of 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> The value of natural gas actually produced in 2013 was US$52.2 million, a 42.7 percent increase over 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-11"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 73</span></sup>\n</p><p>Commercial production of gas from the Songo Songo Island field in the Indian Ocean commenced in 2004, thirty years after it was discovered there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EABrief_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-EABrief-125">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWURA-Ng_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-EWURA-Ng-126">[124]</a></sup> Over 35 billion cubic feet of gas was produced from this field in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-12"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 72</span></sup> with proven, probable, and possible reserves totalling 1.1 trillion cubic feet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWURA-Ng_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-EWURA-Ng-126">[124]</a></sup> The gas is transported by pipeline to Dar es Salaam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EABrief_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-EABrief-125">[123]</a></sup> As of 27 August 2014, TANESCO owed the operator of this field, Orca Exploration Group Inc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A newer natural gas field in Mnazi Bay in 2013 produced about one-seventh of the amount produced near Songo Songo Island<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-13"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 73</span></sup> but has proven, probable, and possible reserves of 2.2 trillion cubic feet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EWURA-Ng_126-2"><a href="#cite_note-EWURA-Ng-126">[124]</a></sup> Virtually all of that gas is being used for electricity generation in <a href="/wiki/Mtwara" title="Mtwara">Mtwara</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EABrief_125-2"><a href="#cite_note-EABrief-125">[123]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Ruvuma and Nyuna regions of Tanzania have been explored mostly by the discovery company that holds a 75 percent interest, Aminex, and has shown to hold in excess of 3.5 trillion cubic feet of natural gas. A pipeline connecting offshore natural gas fields to Tanzania\'s commercial capital Dar es Salaam was completed at the end of April 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Tanzania" title="Tourism in Tanzania">Tourism in Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG/220px-Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG/330px-Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG/440px-Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Uhuru_Peak_Mt._Kilimanjaro_1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The snowcapped <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uhuru_Peak" title="Uhuru Peak">Uhuru Peak</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Travel and tourism contributed 17.5 percent of Tanzania\'s gross domestic product in 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-129">[127]</a></sup> and employed 11.0 percent of the country\'s labour force (1,189,300 jobs) in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knoema_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Knoema-130">[128]</a></sup> Overall receipts rose from US$1.74 billion in 2004 to US$4.48 billion in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knoema_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-Knoema-130">[128]</a></sup> and receipts from international tourists rose from US$1.255 billion in 2010 to US$2 billion in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-129">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> In 2016, 1,284,279 tourists arrived at Tanzania\'s borders compared to 590,000 in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UND_106-2"><a href="#cite_note-UND-106">[104]</a></sup> The vast majority of tourists visit Zanzibar or a "northern circuit" of <a href="/wiki/Serengeti_National_Park" title="Serengeti National Park">Serengeti National Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ngorongoro_Conservation_Area" title="Ngorongoro Conservation Area">Ngorongoro Conservation Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarangire_National_Park" title="Tarangire National Park">Tarangire National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Manyara_National_Park" title="Lake Manyara National Park">Lake Manyara National Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kilimanjaro" title="Mount Kilimanjaro">Mount Kilimanjaro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-11"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1252</span></sup> In 2013, the most visited national park was Serengeti (452,485 tourists), followed by Manyara (187,773) and Tarangire (165,949).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Abstract_45-14"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-45">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page xx</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking">Banking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Banking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Tanzania" title="Bank of Tanzania">Bank of Tanzania</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> of Tanzania and is primarily responsible for maintaining price stability, with a subsidiary responsibility for issuing <a href="/wiki/Tanzanian_shilling" title="Tanzanian shilling">Tanzanian shilling</a> notes and coins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> At the end of 2013, the total assets of the Tanzanian banking industry were 19.5 trillion Tanzanian shillings, a 15 percent increase over 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Tanzania" title="Transport in Tanzania">Transport in Tanzania</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trunk_road_Tanzania.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="533" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Trunk_road_Tanzania.jpg/180px-Trunk_road_Tanzania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Trunk_road_Tanzania.jpg/270px-Trunk_road_Tanzania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Trunk_road_Tanzania.jpg/360px-Trunk_road_Tanzania.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">One of the main trunk roads</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Songwe_Airport.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Songwe_Airport.jpg/180px-Songwe_Airport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Songwe_Airport.jpg/270px-Songwe_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Songwe_Airport.jpg/360px-Songwe_Airport.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Air_Tanzania" title="Air Tanzania">Air Tanzania</a> is the country\'s <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Most transport in Tanzania is by road, with road transport constituting over 75 percent of the country\'s freight traffic and 80 percent of its passenger traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-12"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1252</span></sup> The 86,500 kilometres (53,700&#160;mi) road system is in generally poor condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-13"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1252</span></sup> Tanzania has two railway companies: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TAZARA" title="TAZARA">TAZARA</a>, which provides service between Dar es Salaam and <a href="/wiki/Kapiri_Mposhi" title="Kapiri Mposhi">Kapiri Mposhi</a> (in a copper-mining district in Zambia), and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_Railways_Limited" title="Tanzania Railways Limited">Tanzania Railways Limited</a>, which connects Dar es Salaam with central and northern Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-14"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1252</span></sup> Rail travel in Tanzania often entails slow journeys with frequent cancellations or delays, and the railways have a deficient safety record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-15"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1252</span></sup>\n</p><p>In Dar es Salaam, there is a huge project of rapid buses, <a href="/wiki/Dar_Rapid_Transit_Agency" title="Dar Rapid Transit Agency">Dar Rapid Transit (DART)</a> which connects suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a> city. The development of the DART system consists of six phases and is funded by the African Development Bank, the World Bank and the Government of Tanzania. The first phase began in April 2012, and it was completed in December 2015 and launched operations in May 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania has four international airports, along with over 100 small airports or landing strips. Airport infrastructure tends to be in poor condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-16"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1253</span></sup> Airlines in Tanzania include <a href="/wiki/Air_Tanzania" title="Air Tanzania">Air Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Precision_Air" title="Precision Air">Precision Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fastjet" title="Fastjet">Fastjet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coastal_Aviation" title="Coastal Aviation">Coastal Aviation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ZanAir" title="ZanAir">ZanAir</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-17"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1253</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Tanzania" title="Telecommunications in Tanzania">Telecommunications in Tanzania</a></div>\n<p>In 2013, the communications sector was the fastest growing in Tanzania, expanding 22.8 percent; however, the sector accounted for only 2.4 percent of gross domestic product that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BudEx_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-BudEx-118">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 2</span></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2011, Tanzania had 56 mobile telephone subscribers per 100 inhabitants, a rate slightly above the sub-Saharan average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-18"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1253</span></sup> Very few Tanzanians have fixed-line telephones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-19"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1253</span></sup> Approximately 12 percent of Tanzanians used the internet as of  2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, though this number is growing rapidly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-20"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1253</span></sup> The country has a fibre-optic cable network that replaced unreliable satellite service, but internet bandwidth remains very low.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-21"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1253</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Tanzania" title="Water supply and sanitation in Tanzania">Water supply and sanitation in Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa,_2012_or_closest_year.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="232" decoding="async" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa%2C_2012_or_closest_year.svg/220px-Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa%2C_2012_or_closest_year.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa%2C_2012_or_closest_year.svg/330px-Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa%2C_2012_or_closest_year.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa%2C_2012_or_closest_year.svg/440px-Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa%2C_2012_or_closest_year.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gross_domestic_expenditure_on_Research_and_Development_GDP_ratio_in_Southern_Africa,_2012_or_closest_year.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Domestic expenditure on research in Southern Africa as a percentage of GDP, 2012 or closest year. Source: UNESCO Science Report: towards 2030 (2015), Figure 20.3</div></div></div>\n<p>Water supply and sanitation in Tanzania has been characterised by decreasing access to <a href="/wiki/Improved_water_source" title="Improved water source">improved water sources</a> in the 2000s (especially in urban areas), steady access to some form of sanitation (around 93 percent since the 1990s), intermittent water supplies, and generally low quality of service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mowi_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-mowi-135">[133]</a></sup> Many utilities are barely able to cover their operation and maintenance costs through revenues because of low tariffs and poor efficiency. There are significant <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Tanzania" title="Regions of Tanzania">regional</a> differences, with the best performing utilities being <a href="/wiki/Arusha" title="Arusha">Arusha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moshi,_Tanzania" title="Moshi, Tanzania">Moshi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tanga,_Tanzania" title="Tanga, Tanzania">Tanga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pubexp_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-pubexp-136">[134]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government of Tanzania has embarked on a major sector reform process since 2002. An ambitious National Water Sector Development Strategy that promotes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integrated_Water_Resources_Management" title="Integrated Water Resources Management">integrated water resources management</a> and the development of urban and rural water supply was adopted in 2006. Decentralisation has meant that responsibility for water and sanitation service provision has shifted to local government authorities and is carried out by 20 urban utilities and about 100 district utilities, as well as by Community Owned Water Supply Organisations in rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mowi_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-mowi-135">[133]</a></sup>\n</p><p>These reforms have been backed by a significant increase of the budget starting in 2006, when the water sector was included among the priority sectors of the National Strategy for Growth and Reduction of Poverty . The Tanzanian water sector remains heavily dependent on external donors, with 88 percent of the available funds being provided by external donor organisations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWSDS_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-NWSDS-137">[135]</a></sup> Results have been mixed. For example, a report by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Gesellschaft_f%C3%BCr_Internationale_Zusammenarbeit" title="Deutsche Gesellschaft f&#252;r Internationale Zusammenarbeit">Deutsche Gesellschaft f&#252;r Internationale Zusammenarbeit</a> noted that "despite heavy investments brought in by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, (the utility serving <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>) has remained one of the worst performing water entities in Tanzania."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GIZ_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-GIZ-138">[136]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_nutrition">Food and nutrition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Food and nutrition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:255px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pilua_for_many.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3610" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Pilua_for_many.jpg/253px-Pilua_for_many.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Pilua_for_many.jpg/380px-Pilua_for_many.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Pilua_for_many.jpg/506px-Pilua_for_many.jpg 2x" width="253"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pilua_for_many.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Tanzanian woman cooks Pilau rice dish wearing traditional <a href="/wiki/Kanga_(African_garment)" title="Kanga (African garment)">Kanga</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Poor nutrition remains a persistent problem within Tanzania and varies hugely throughout the country\'s regions. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">USAID</a> reports that 16% of children are underweight and 34% experience stunted growth as a result of malnutrition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-:02-139">[137]</a></sup> 10 regions house 58% of children suffering from stunted growth while 50% of acutely malnourished children can be found in 5 regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-140">[138]</a></sup> Over a 5-year period, the <a href="/wiki/Mara_Region" title="Mara Region">Mara</a> district of Tanzania saw a 15% reduction in stunting in children under 5 years old, falling from 46% to 31% in 2005 and 2010 respectively. <a href="/wiki/Dodoma" title="Dodoma">Dodoma</a>, on the other hand saw a 7% increase in the prevalence of stunting in this age group, rising from 50% in 2005 to 57% in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-141">[139]</a></sup> Overall availability of food does not necessarily contribute to overall stunting figures. <a href="/wiki/Iringa_Region" title="Iringa Region">Iringa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbeya_Region" title="Mbeya Region">Mbeya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rukwa_Region" title="Rukwa Region">Rukwa</a> regions, where overall availability of food is considered acceptable still experience stunting incidences in excess of 50%. In some areas where food shortages are common such as in the <a href="/wiki/Tabora_Region" title="Tabora Region">Tabora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singida_Region" title="Singida Region">Singida</a> regions, stunting incidences remain comparatively less than those seen in Iringa, Mbeya and Rukwa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-141">[139]</a></sup> The Tanzania Food and Nutrition Centre attributes these discrepancies to variance in maternal malnutrition, poor infant feeding practices, hygiene practices and poor healthcare services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_141-2"><a href="#cite_note-:6-141">[139]</a></sup> Periods of drought can have significant impacts on the production of crops in Tanzania. Drought in East Africa has resulted in massive increases in the prices of food staples such as <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commercial_sorghum" title="Commercial sorghum">sorghum</a>, crops crucial to the nutrition of the majority of Tanzania\'s population. From 2015 to 2017, the price of maize when bought wholesale has more than doubled from 400 <a href="/wiki/Tanzanian_shilling" title="Tanzanian shilling">Shillings</a> per kilogram to 1253 Shillings per kilogram respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:256px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Farmers_in_Igunga,_Tanzania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1080" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Farmers_in_Igunga%2C_Tanzania.jpg/254px-Farmers_in_Igunga%2C_Tanzania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Farmers_in_Igunga%2C_Tanzania.jpg/381px-Farmers_in_Igunga%2C_Tanzania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Farmers_in_Igunga%2C_Tanzania.jpg/508px-Farmers_in_Igunga%2C_Tanzania.jpg 2x" width="254"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Farmers_in_Igunga,_Tanzania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Farmers in Igunga District, Tanzania</div></div></div>\n<p>Tanzania remains heavily agricultural, with 80% of the total population engaging in subsistence farming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-:12-143">[141]</a></sup> Rural areas are subjected to increased food shortages in comparison to urbanized areas, with a survey carried out within the country in 2017 finding 84% of people in rural areas suffering food shortages over a 3-month period compared to 64% of residents in cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-:12-143">[141]</a></sup> This disparity between rural and city nutrition can be attributed to various factors; increased nutritional needs due to manual labor, more limited access to food as a result of poor infrastructure, high-susceptibility to the damaging effects of nature and the "Agricultural Productivity Gap".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> The Agricultural Productivity Gap postulates that "value added per worker" is often much lower within the agricultural sector than that found within non-agricultural sectors. Furthermore, allocation of labor within the agricultural sector is largely allocated ineffectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Programs_targeting_hunger">Programs targeting hunger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Programs targeting hunger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Currently various USAID programs focusing on nutrition operate within the <a href="/wiki/Morogoro" title="Morogoro">Morogoro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dodoma" title="Dodoma">Dodoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iringa" title="Iringa">Iringa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbeya" title="Mbeya">Mbeya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manyara_Region" title="Manyara Region">Manyara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songwe_Region" title="Songwe Region">Songwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> regions of Tanzania. These "<a href="/wiki/Feed_the_Future_Initiative" title="Feed the Future Initiative">Feed the Future</a>" programs heavily invest in nutrition, infrastructure, policy, capacity of institutions and agriculture which is identified by the organization as a key area of economic growth in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:02_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-:02-139">[137]</a></sup> A Tanzanian government led initiative "Kilimo Kwanza" or "Agriculture First" aims to encourage investment into agriculture within the private sector and hopes to improve agricultural processes and development within the country by seeking the knowledge of young people and the innovation that they can potentially provide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-146">[144]</a></sup> During the 1990s, around 25% of Tanzania\'s population were provided access to iodized oil aimed to target iodine deficiency within expecting mothers, as result of studies showing the negative effects of in-utero iodine deficiency on cognitive development in children. Research showed that children of mothers with access to the supplement achieved on average greater than a third of a year more education than those who did not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-146">[144]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:255px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg/253px-Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg/380px-Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg/506px-Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg 2x" width="253"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Food_Items_in_World_Food_Programme_Food_Parcels.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Example of a World Food Programme parcel</div></div></div>\n<p>Various programmes led by the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> currently operate within Tanzania. The Supplementary Feeding Program (SFP) aims to target acute malnutrition by supplying blended food fortified with vitamins to pregnant women and mothers to children under 5 on a monthly basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-147">[145]</a></sup> Pregnant women and mothers to children under 2 have access to the Mother and Child Health and Nutrition Programme\'s "Super Cereal" which is supplied with the intent of reducing stunting in children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-147">[145]</a></sup> World Food Programme supplementation remains the main food source for Tanzania\'s refugees. Super Cereal, Vegetable Oil, Pulses and Salt are supplied as part of the Protracted Relief and Recovery Operation in order to meet the average persons minimum daily calorific requirement of 2,100 kcal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-:4-147">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> state that continued investment in nutrition within Tanzania is of the utmost importance: Estimates predict that Tanzania stands to lose $20 billion by 2025 if nutrition within the country remains at its current level, however improvements in nutrition could produce a gain of around $4.7 billion<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-140">[138]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Save the Children, with the help of UNICEF and <a href="/wiki/Irish_Aid" title="Irish Aid">Irish Aid</a> funding created the Partnership for Nutrition in Tanzania (PANITA), in 2011. PANITA aims to utilize civil society organizations to specifically target nutrition within the country. Alongside this, various sectors associated with nutrition are targeted such as agriculture, water, sanitation, education, economic development and social progress. PANITA is responsible for ensuring significant attention is given to nutrition in development plans and budgets created on national and regional levels within Tanzania. Since its conception, PANITA has grown from 94 to 306 participating civil society organizations nationwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-148">[146]</a></sup> Agriculture within Tanzania is specifically targeted by the Irish Aid led initiative Harnessing Agriculture for Nutrition Outcomes (HANO), which aims to merge nutrition initiatives with agriculture in the Lindi District of the country. The project aims to reduce stunting by 10% in children aged 0 to 23 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-148">[146]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Researchers_(HC)_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants,_2013_or_closest_year.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="232" decoding="async" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Researchers_%28HC%29_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants%2C_2013_or_closest_year.svg/220px-Researchers_%28HC%29_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants%2C_2013_or_closest_year.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Researchers_%28HC%29_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants%2C_2013_or_closest_year.svg/330px-Researchers_%28HC%29_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants%2C_2013_or_closest_year.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Researchers_%28HC%29_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants%2C_2013_or_closest_year.svg/440px-Researchers_%28HC%29_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants%2C_2013_or_closest_year.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Researchers_(HC)_in_Southern_Africa_per_million_inhabitants,_2013_or_closest_year.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Researchers (HC) in Southern Africa per million inhabitants, 2013 or closest year</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Tanzania" title="Science and technology in Tanzania">Science and technology in Tanzania</a></div>\n<p>Tanzania\'s first "National Science and Technology Policy" was adopted in 1996. The objective of the government\'s "Vision 2025" (1998) document was to "transform the economy into a strong, resilient and competitive one, buttressed by science and technology".\n</p><p>Under the umbrella of the One UN Initiative, UNESCO and Tanzanian government departments and agencies formulated a series of proposals in 2008 for revising the "National Science and Technology Policy". The total reform budget of US$10 million was financed from the One UN fund and other sources. UNESCO provided support for mainstreaming science, technology, and innovation into the new "National Growth and Poverty Reduction Strategy" for the mainland and Zanzibar namely, Mkukuta II and Mkuza II, including in the field of tourism.\n</p><p>Tanzania\'s revised science policy was published in 2010. Entitled "National Research and Development Policy", it recognizes the need to improve the process of prioritization of research capacities, develop international co-operation in strategic areas of research and development, and improve planning for human resources. It also makes provisions for the establishment of a National Research Fund. This policy was, in turn, reviewed in 2012 and 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-149">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="176" data-file-width="511" decoding="async" height="76" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg/220px-Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg/330px-Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg/440px-Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seychelles_and_South_Africa_have_the_most_publications_per_million_inhabitants.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scientific&#160;publications per million inhabitants in SADC countries in 2014. Source: UNESCO Science Report (2015), data from Thomson Reuters\' Web of Science, Science Citation Index Expanded</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2010, Tanzania devoted 0.38 percent of GDP to research and development. The global average in 2013 was 1.7 percent of GDP. Tanzania had 69 researchers (in head counts) per million population in 2010. In 2014, Tanzania counted 15 publications per million inhabitants in internationally catalogued journals, according to Thomson Reuters\' Web of Science (Science Citation Index Expanded). The average for sub-Saharan Africa was 20 publications per million inhabitants and the global average 176 publications per million inhabitants.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Tanzania" title="Demographics of Tanzania">Demographics of Tanzania</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<caption>Population in Tanzania<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-7">[7]</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col" style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th scope="col" style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">7.9\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">35.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">55.6\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>According to the 2012 census, the total population was 44,928,923.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012_census_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-2012_census-8">[8]</a></sup> The under-15 age group represented 44.1 percent of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbs1_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbs1-150">[148]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The population distribution in Tanzania is uneven. Most people live on the northern border or the eastern coast, with much of the remainder of the country being sparsely populated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frame_56-22"><a href="#cite_note-frame-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1252</span></sup> Density varies from 12 per square kilometre (31/sq&#160;mi) in the <a href="/wiki/Katavi_Region" title="Katavi Region">Katavi Region</a> to 3,133 per square kilometre (8,110/sq&#160;mi) in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam_Region" title="Dar es Salaam Region">Dar es Salaam Region</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012_census_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-2012_census-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 6</span></sup>\n</p><p>Approximately 70 percent of the population is rural, although this percentage has been declining since at least 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> Dar es Salaam (population 4,364,541)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2012_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-census2012-152">[150]</a></sup> is the largest city and commercial capital. <a href="/wiki/Dodoma" title="Dodoma">Dodoma</a> (population 2,083,588)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2012_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-census2012-152">[150]</a></sup> is located in the centre of Tanzania, is the capital of the country, and hosts the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>.\n</p><p><br/>\n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th class="navbox-title" colspan="10"><div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div><div class="plainlinks hlist template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div> <div style="height:2.6em;line-height:1.3em;"><span style="font-size:110%;">Largest cities or towns in Tanzania</span><br/><div rel="nofollow">2012 Census General Report, March 2013 Combined Final for Printing</a></div></div>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th></th>\n<th>Rank\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Tanzania" title="List of cities in Tanzania">Name</a>\n</th>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Tanzania" title="Regions of Tanzania">Region</a>\n</th>\n<th>Pop.\n</th>\n<th>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="11" class="image" href="/wiki/File:Look_at_Mt._Meru_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg" title="Arusha"><img alt="Arusha" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1822" data-file-width="2743" decoding="async" height="80" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Look_at_Mt._Meru_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg/240px-Look_at_Mt._Meru_Arusha_Tanzania.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a><br/><a href="/wiki/Arusha" title="Mbeya Region">Mbeya</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">385,279\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">6</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a
