style="text-align:right;">315,866\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">7</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tanga,_Tanzania" title="Tanga, Tanzania">Tanga</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tanga_Region" title="Tanga Region">Tanga</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">273,332\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">8</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Kahama,_Tanzania" title="Kahama, Tanzania">Kahama</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Shinyanga_Region" title="Shinyanga Region">Shinyanga</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">242,208\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">9</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tabora" title="Tabora">Tabora</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Tabora_Region" title="Tabora Region">Tabora</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">226,999\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_City" title="Zanzibar City">Zanzibar City</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zanzibar_West_Region" title="Zanzibar West Region">Zanzibar West</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">223,033\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg/220px-Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg/330px-Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg/440px-Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hadzabe_Hunters.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Hadza_people" title="Hadza people">Hadza</a> live as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherers" title="Hunter-gatherers">hunter-gatherers</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The population consists of <a href="/wiki/List_of_ethnic_groups_in_Tanzania" title="List of ethnic groups in Tanzania">about 125 ethnic groups</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lev_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-lev-153">[151]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sukuma_people" title="Sukuma people">Sukuma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nyamwezi_people" title="Nyamwezi people">Nyamwezi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaga_people" title="Chaga people">Chagga</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Haya_people" title="Haya people">Haya</a> peoples each have a population exceeding 1 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 4</span></sup> Approximately 99 percent of Tanzanians are of African descent, with small numbers of Arab, European, and Asian descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lev_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-lev-153">[151]</a></sup> The majority of Tanzanians, including the Sukuma and the Nyamwezi, are <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The population also includes people of Arab, Persian, and <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Tanzania" title="Indians in Tanzania">Indian</a> origin, and small European and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Tanzania" title="Chinese people in Tanzania">Chinese</a> communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> Many also identify as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shirazi_(ethnic_group)" title="Shirazi (ethnic group)">Shirazis</a>. Thousands of Arabs, Persians, and Indians were massacred during the <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Revolution" title="Zanzibar Revolution">Zanzibar Revolution</a> of 1964.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar-46">[44]</a></sup> As of 1994, the Asian community numbered 50,000 on the mainland and 4,000 on Zanzibar. An estimated 70,000 Arabs and 10,000 Europeans lived in Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pop_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-pop-157">[155]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albinos" title="Albinos">albinos</a> in Tanzania have been the victims of violence in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> Attacks are often to hack off the limbs of albinos in the perverse superstitious belief that possessing the bones of albinos will bring wealth. The country has banned witch doctors to try to prevent the practice, but it has continued and albinos remain targets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to 2010 Tanzanian government statistics, the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in Tanzania was 5.4 children born per woman, with 3.7 in urban mainland areas, 6.1 in rural mainland areas, and 5.1 in Zanzibar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-163">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 55</span></sup> For all women aged 45&#8211;49, 37.3 percent had given birth to eight or more children, and for currently married women in that age group, 45.0 percent had given birth to that many children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-163">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 61</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:250px; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:none"><th colspan="5" style="text-align:center;">Religion in <b>Tanzania</b> (2014)</th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:DodgerBlue; width:61.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">61.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:MediumSeaGreen; width:35.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">35.2%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religion" title="Traditional African religion">Indigenous beliefs</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:red; width:1.8%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.8%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">Other</a></td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:yellow; width:1.6%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr><td colspan="5" style="padding:5px; text-align:left;">Source: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-19">[17]</a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dar_es_Salaam-Azania_Front.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="577" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dar_es_Salaam-Azania_Front.jpg/190px-Dar_es_Salaam-Azania_Front.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dar_es_Salaam-Azania_Front.jpg/285px-Dar_es_Salaam-Azania_Front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Dar_es_Salaam-Azania_Front.jpg/380px-Dar_es_Salaam-Azania_Front.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Azania_Front_Lutheran_Church" title="Azania Front Lutheran Church">Azania Front Lutheran Church</a>, built by German missionaries in 1898</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gaddafi_Mosque.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Gaddafi_Mosque.jpg/190px-Gaddafi_Mosque.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Gaddafi_Mosque.jpg/285px-Gaddafi_Mosque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Gaddafi_Mosque.jpg/380px-Gaddafi_Mosque.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Gaddafi_Mosque" title="Gaddafi Mosque">Gaddafi Mosque</a> in the capital <a href="/wiki/Dodoma" title="Dodoma">Dodoma</a> is the second-largest mosque in East Africa.</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Tanzania" title="Religion in Tanzania">Religion in Tanzania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Zanzibar" title="Islam in Zanzibar">Islam in Zanzibar</a></div>\n<p>Official statistics on religion are unavailable because religious surveys were eliminated from government census reports after 1967. Religious leaders and sociologists estimated in 2007 that <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> communities were approximately equal in size, each accounting for 30 to 40 percent of the population, with the remainder consisting of practitioners of other faiths, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_traditional_religions" title="African traditional religions">indigenous religions</a>, and people of "<a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religion</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-report_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-report-164">[162]</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to a 2014 estimate by the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a></i>, 61.4 percent of the population was Christian, 35.2 percent was Muslim, 1.8 percent practiced traditional African religions, 1.4 percent were unaffiliated with any religion, and 0.2 followed other religions. Nearly the entire population of Zanzibar is Muslim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_19-5"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-19">[17]</a></sup> Of Muslims, 16 percent are <a href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya" title="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</a> (although they are often not considered Muslims), 20 percent are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a>, 40 percent are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunni" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>, 20 percent are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shia" title="Shia">Shia</a>, and 4% are Sufi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Christian population is mostly composed of Roman Catholics and Protestants. Among Protestants, the large number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravians</a> points to the German past of the country, while the number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicans" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a> point to the British history of Tanganyika. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostals" title="Pentecostals">Pentecostals</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adventists" title="Adventists">Adventists</a> are also present because of missionary activity. All of them have had some influence in varying degrees from the Walokole movement (East African Revival), which has also been fertile ground for the spread of charismatic and Pentecostal groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are also active communities of other religious groups, primarily on the mainland, such as Buddhists, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Tanzania" title="Hinduism in Tanzania">Hindus</a>, and Bah&#225;\'&#237;s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Tanzania" title="Languages of Tanzania">Languages of Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg/170px-Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg/255px-Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg/340px-Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zanzibar_door_carved.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A carved door with Arabic calligraphy in Zanzibar</div></div></div>\n<p>More than 100 <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Tanzania" title="Languages of Tanzania">languages are spoken in Tanzania</a>, making it the most linguistically diverse country in East Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup> Among the languages spoken are all four of Africa\'s language families: <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_languages" title="Nilotic languages">Nilotic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">Khoisan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-4"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup> There are no <i>de jure</i> official languages in Tanzania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tzgov_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-tzgov-25">[23]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Swahili is used in parliamentary debate, in the lower courts, and as a medium of instruction in primary school. English is used in foreign trade, in diplomacy, in higher courts, and as a medium of instruction in secondary and higher education,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-5"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup> The Tanzanian government, however, has plans to discontinue English as a language of instruction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afkinsider.com_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-afkinsider.com-26">[24]</a></sup> In connection with his Ujamaa social policies, President Nyerere encouraged the use of Swahili to help unify the country\'s many ethnic groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Joshua_A._Fishman_Distinguished_University_Research_Professor_of_Social_Sciences_Yeshiva_University_Emeritus_2001_361_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Joshua_A._Fishman_Distinguished_University_Research_Professor_of_Social_Sciences_Yeshiva_University_Emeritus_2001_361-168">[166]</a></sup> Approximately 10 percent of Tanzanians speak Swahili as a first language, and up to 90 percent speak it as a second language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-6"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup> Many educated Tanzanians are trilingual, also speaking English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Quintin_Winks_2011_145_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Quintin_Winks_2011_145-169">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bj_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-bj-170">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fran&#231;ois_Grosjean_1982_8_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fran&#231;ois_Grosjean_1982_8-171">[169]</a></sup> The widespread use and promotion of Swahili is contributing to the decline of smaller languages in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sim_24-7"><a href="#cite_note-sim-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Matthias_Brenzinger_1992_86_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Matthias_Brenzinger_1992_86-172">[170]</a></sup> Young children increasingly speak Swahili as a first language, particularly in urban areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elsevier_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elsevier-173">[171]</a></sup> Ethnic community languages (ECL) other than Kiswahili are not allowed as a language of instruction. Nor are they taught as a subject, though they might be used unofficially in some cases in initial education. Television and radio programmes in an ECL are prohibited, and it is nearly impossible to get permission to publish a newspaper in an ECL. There is no department of local or regional African Languages and Literatures at the University of Dar es Salaam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> is co-official in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sandawe_people" title="Sandawe people">Sandawe people</a> speak a language that may be related to the <a href="/wiki/Khoe_languages" title="Khoe languages">Khoe languages</a> of Botswana and Namibia, while the language of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hadzabe_people" title="Hadzabe people">Hadzabe people</a>, although it has similar <a href="/wiki/Click_consonant" title="Click consonant">click consonants</a>, is arguably a <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolate</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> The language of the <a href="/wiki/Iraqw_people" title="Iraqw people">Iraqw people</a> is Cushitic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Tanzania" title="Education in Tanzania">Education in Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nkrumah.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2576" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nkrumah.JPG/220px-Nkrumah.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nkrumah.JPG/330px-Nkrumah.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nkrumah.JPG/440px-Nkrumah.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nkrumah.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nkrumah Hall at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dar_es_Salaam" title="University of Dar es Salaam">University of Dar es Salaam</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 2012, the literacy rate in Tanzania for persons aged 15 and over was estimated to be 67.8 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> Education is compulsory until children reach age 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worst_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-worst-178">[176]</a></sup> In 2010, 74.1 percent of children age 5 to 14 years were attending school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worst_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-worst-178">[176]</a></sup> The primary school completion rate was 80.8 percent in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worst_178-2"><a href="#cite_note-worst-178">[176]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Tanzania" title="Healthcare in Tanzania">Healthcare in Tanzania</a></div>\n<p>As of  2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, life expectancy at birth was 61 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-who-179">[177]</a></sup> The under-five mortality rate in 2012 was 54 per 1,000 live births.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who_179-1"><a href="#cite_note-who-179">[177]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate in 2013 was estimated at 410 per 100,000 live births.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who_179-2"><a href="#cite_note-who-179">[177]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premature_death" title="Premature death">Prematurity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> were tied in 2010 as the leading cause of death in children under 5 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013-180">[178]</a></sup> The other leading causes of death for these children were, in decreasing order, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diarrhoea" title="Diarrhoea">diarrhoea</a>, <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013-180">[178]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Malaria in Tanzania causes death and disease and has a "huge economic impact".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Progress_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Progress-181">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 13</span></sup> There were approximately 11.5 million cases of clinical malaria in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Progress_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-Progress-181">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 12</span></sup> In 2007&#8211;08, malaria prevalence among children aged 6 months to 5 years was highest in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kagera_Region" title="Kagera Region">Kagera Region</a> (41.1 percent) on the western shore of Lake Victoria and lowest in the <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Region" title="Arusha Region">Arusha Region</a> (0.1 percent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Progress_181-2"><a href="#cite_note-Progress-181">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 12</span></sup>\n</p><p>According to the 2010 <i>Tanzania Demographic and Health Survey 2010</i>, 15 percent of Tanzanian women had undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> (FGM)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_163-2"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-163">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 295</span></sup> and 72 percent of Tanzanian men had been circumcised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_163-3"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-163">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 230</span></sup> FGM is most common in the <a href="/wiki/Manyara_Region" title="Manyara Region">Manyara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dodoma_Region" title="Dodoma Region">Dodoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Region" title="Arusha Region">Arusha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Singida_Region" title="Singida Region">Singida</a> regions and nonexistent in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_163-4"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-163">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 296</span></sup> The prevalence of male circumcision was above 90 percent in the eastern (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam_Region" title="Dar es Salaam Region">Dar es Salaam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pwani_Region" title="Pwani Region">Pwani</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morogoro_Region" title="Morogoro Region">Morogoro</a> regions), northern (<a href="/wiki/Kilimanjaro_Region" title="Kilimanjaro Region">Kilimanjaro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanga_Region" title="Tanga Region">Tanga</a>, Arusha, and Manyara regions), and central areas (Dodoma and <a href="/wiki/Singida_Region" title="Singida Region">Singida</a> regions) and below 50 percent only in the southern highlands zone (<a href="/wiki/Mbeya_Region" title="Mbeya Region">Mbeya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iringa_Region" title="Iringa Region">Iringa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rukwa_Region" title="Rukwa Region">Rukwa</a> regions).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHS_163-5"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-163">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>pages 6, 230</span></sup>\n</p><p>2012 data showed that 53 percent of the population used improved drinking water sources (defined as a source that "by nature of its construction and design, is likely to protect the source from outside contamination, in particular from faecal matter") and 12 percent used improved sanitation facilities (defined as facilities that "likely hygienically separates human excreta from human contact" but not including facilities shared with other households or open to public use).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="HIV.2FAIDS"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: HIV/AIDS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Tanzania" title="HIV/AIDS in Tanzania">HIV/AIDS in Tanzania</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> estimated in 2012 that the prevalence of HIV was 3.1 percent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-who_179-3"><a href="#cite_note-who-179">[177]</a></sup> although the <i>Tanzania HIV/AIDS and Malaria Indicator Survey 2011&#8211;12</i> found that, on average, 5.1 percent of those tested in the 15 to 49 age group were HIV-positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antiretroviral_drug" title="Antiretroviral drug">Anti-retroviral</a> treatment coverage for people living with HIV was 37 percent in 2013, compared to 19 percent in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup> According to a 2013 report published by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_United_Nations_Programme_on_HIV_and_AIDS" title="Joint United Nations Programme on HIV and AIDS">Joint United Nations Programme on HIV and AIDS</a> that compares 2012 with 2001 data, AIDS deaths have decreased 33 percent, new HIV infections have decreased 36 percent, and new HIV infections among children have decreased 67 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Women_in_Tanzania" title="Women in Tanzania">Women in Tanzania</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Woman" title="Woman">Women</a> and <a href="/wiki/Man" title="Man">men</a> have equality for the law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\nThe government signed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_against_Women" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women">Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women</a> (CEDAW) in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-1"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\nNearly 3 out of ten females reported having experienced <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a> before the age of 18.\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-2"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup> The prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> has decreased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-3"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\nSchool girls are reinstated back to school after delivery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-4"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">Police</a> Force administration strives to separate the Gender Desks from normal police operations to enhance confidentiality of the processing of women victims of abuse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-5"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\nMost of the abuses and violence against women and children occurs at the <a href="/wiki/Family" title="Family">family</a> level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-6"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Tanzania" title="Constitution of Tanzania">Constitution of Tanzania</a> requires that women to constitute at least 30% of all elected members of <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-7"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup> The gender differences in education and training have implications later in life of these women and girls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-8"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">Unemployment</a> is higher for females than for males.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-9"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup> The right of a female employee to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternity_leave" title="Maternity leave">maternity leave</a> is guaranteed in labour law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cedaw_186-10"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-186">[184]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Tanzania" title="Culture of Tanzania">Culture of Tanzania</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Judith_Wambura,.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1037" data-file-width="1556" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg/220px-Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg/330px-Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg/440px-Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Judith_Wambura,.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lady_Jaydee" title="Lady Jaydee">Judith Wambura (Lady Jaydee)</a> is a popular Bongo Flava recording singer.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tanzanian_literature" title="Tanzanian literature">Tanzanian literature</a></div>\n<p>Tanzania\'s literary culture is primarily oral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 68</span></sup> Major oral literary forms include folktales, poems, riddles, proverbs, and songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 69</span></sup> The greatest part of Tanzania\'s recorded oral literature is in Swahili, even though each of the country\'s languages has its own oral tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-3"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>pages 68&#8211;9</span></sup> The country\'s oral literature has been declining because of the breakdown of the multigenerational social structure, making transmission of oral literature more difficult, and because increasing modernisation has been accompanied by the devaluation of oral literature.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-4"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 69</span></sup>\n</p><p>Tanzania\'s written literary tradition is relatively undeveloped. Tanzania does not have a lifelong reading culture, and books are often expensive and hard to come by.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-5"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 75</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doling_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-187">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 16</span></sup> Most Tanzanian literature is in Swahili or English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-6"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 75</span></sup> Major figures in Tanzanian written literature include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaaban_Robert" title="Shaaban Robert">Shaaban Robert</a> (considered the father of Swahili literature), Muhammed Saley Farsy, Faraji Katalambulla, Adam Shafi Adam, Muhammed Said Abdalla, Said Ahmed Mohammed Khamis, Mohamed Suleiman Mohamed, <a href="/wiki/Euphrase_Kezilahabi" title="Euphrase Kezilahabi">Euphrase Kezilahabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Ruhumbika" title="Gabriel Ruhumbika">Gabriel Ruhumbika</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ebrahim_Hussein" title="Ebrahim Hussein">Ebrahim Hussein</a>, May Materru Balisidya, <a href="/wiki/Fadhy_Mtanga" title="Fadhy Mtanga">Fadhy Mtanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdulrazak_Gurnah" title="Abdulrazak Gurnah">Abdulrazak Gurnah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Penina_Muhando" title="Penina Muhando">Penina O. Mlama</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-7"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>pages 76&#8211;8</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Painting_and_sculpture">Painting and sculpture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Painting and sculpture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Amani-TT4798.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="515" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Amani-TT4798.jpg/220px-Amani-TT4798.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Amani-TT4798.jpg/330px-Amani-TT4798.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Amani-TT4798.jpg/440px-Amani-TT4798.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Amani-TT4798.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Tingatinga_(painting)" title="Tingatinga (painting)">Tingatinga</a> painting</div></div></div>\n<p>Two Tanzanian art styles have achieved international recognition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doling_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-187">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tingatinga_(painting)" title="Tingatinga (painting)">Tingatinga</a> school of painting, founded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edward_Said_Tingatinga" title="Edward Said Tingatinga">Edward Said Tingatinga</a>, consists of brightly coloured enamel paintings on canvas, generally depicting people, animals, or daily life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-8"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 113</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doling_187-2"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-187">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup> After Tingatinga\'s death in 1972, other artists adopted and developed his style, with the genre now being the most important tourist-oriented style in East Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otiso_154-9"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 113</span></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doling_187-3"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-187">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup>\n</p><p>Historically, there were limited opportunities for formal European art training in Tanzania and many aspiring Tanzanian artists left the country to pursue their vocation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Doling_187-4"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-187">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Tanzania" title="Sport in Tanzania">Sport in Tanzania</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is very popular throughout the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wairagala_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wairagala-188">[186]</a></sup> The most popular <a href="/wiki/Tanzanian_Premier_League" title="Tanzanian Premier League">professional football clubs</a> in Dar es Salaam are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Young_Africans_F.C." title="Young Africans F.C.">Young Africans F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simba_S.C." title="Simba S.C.">Simba S.C.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_Football_Federation" title="Tanzania Football Federation">Tanzania Football Federation</a> is the governing body for football in the country.\n</p><p>Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>, boxing, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wairagala_188-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wairagala-188">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[188]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Tanzania has a popular film industry known as "Bongo Movie".\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a id="cite_note-c-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-c_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">+007 from <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> and <a However, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'z\' in \'zoom\'">z</span><span title="/e&#618;/: \'a\' in \'face\'">e&#618;</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span><span title="/./: syllable break">.</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span></span> is also heard in English.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources">Sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Definition_of_Free_Cultural_Works_logo_notext.svg"><img alt="Definition of Free Cultural Works logo notext.svg" data-file-height="218" data-file-width="219" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Definition_of_Free_Cultural_Works_logo_notext.svg/12px-Definition_of_Free_Cultural_Works_logo_notext.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Definition_of_Free_Cultural_Works_logo_notext.svg/18px-Definition_of_Free_Cultural_Works_logo_notext.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Definition_of_Free_Cultural_Works_logo_notext.svg/24px-Definition_of_Free_Cultural_Works_logo_notext.svg.png 2x" width="12"/></a>&#160;This article incorporates text from a <a href="/wiki/Free_content" title="Free content">free content</a> work.
